"Ugh, not again," you spout as the old wagon shutters, then dies. Stranded on the road again, but this time, your money has gone dry. All but your 50 dollar bill that Grandma gave you on her last Christmas. You've been saving it for when you needed it most, but surely, it won't be enough.

The door creaks open, and you step out into the night sky, coughing up the smoke from your fried vehicle. After pushing your car off the road and between the trees, there isn't much else left for you to do, so you begin to wander down the dark, lonely street.

But at the end of the road, where concrete turned to stone turned to dirt, you notice a light up ahead, on the top of a hill. 

As you waltz into the old, wooden shack, your eyes begin to light up with the fire of a thousand suns. Roulette wheels! Poker tables! And in a dark corner of the abandoned casino, sits a dealer, shuffling cards for a new round of Blackjack. That 50 dollars might just come in handy after all. Thanks, Grandma!

As you go to sit down at the table, you hear the Dealer cough, then watch as he sits up.

In a deep, and yet strained voice, the Dealer, cloaked in darkness, poses a question to you.

Would you like to play a game of Blackjack? You have $50

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 2 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
Your eyes pop open and you're ready to go. Did someone slip you a good dream? Because that was chef's kiss.

You can't sleep, so you walk. The city is different at this hour — quieter, more honest, the neon signs humming a frequency that only works on insomniacs and people with nothing left to protect.

You pass closed shops and sleeping houses. Everyone behind those walls has a bed. A fridge. A door that locks from the inside. You walk past all of it without slowing down, because the rhythm is the only thing that works — step, step, step, forward, one direction, don't stop.

When you get back to your car, you're tired in the right way for once. The kind of tired that actually leads to sleep.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 3 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
With energy. Like, real energy. Not 'I didn't die in my sleep' energy.

You step out of your car and nearly collide with... a mime? Full striped shirt, white face paint, the whole nine yards.

The mime stares at you. You stare back.

Without a word (obviously), the mime begins to act out a scene. He's pretending to be trapped in a box. Classic.

Then he mimes... crying? Counting money? Losing at cards?

Wait. Is he acting out YOUR life?

The mime finishes with a dramatic death scene, tongue out and everything, then springs back up and takes a bow.

The mime looks devastated. He mimes a single tear rolling down his cheek, then slowly backs away, never breaking eye contact.

You feel kind of bad about that.



Three AM. Four AM. Five AM. You've watched every hour tick over on the dashboard clock like you're being paid to witness it. Your body is doing that thing where it's so tired it stopped knowing how to sleep.

Your brain is throwing a party. An awful, private party where every guest is a decision you made wrong and the music is the specific silence of a car park at 4 AM. At 5:47 you finally drift off. Your alarm goes off at 6:00.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 5 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
Your body feels like it got a factory reset overnight. Joints? Smooth. Back? Fine. Mood? Immaculate.

You drive your car to a gas station for supplies. Just snacks. Maybe some coffee.

"EVERYBODY ON THE GROUND! NOW!"

A man with a shotgun. Ski mask. Shaking hands. This is really happening.

The cashier freezes. A mother clutches her child. An old man drops his coffee.

The robber swings the gun around, wild-eyed.



You duck behind a shelf. Slowly, carefully, you crawl toward the back.

The robber is focused on the register. You're almost to the storage room...

You make it. Hide behind boxes of toilet paper and canned goods.

You can hear everything. The shouting. The crying. The crash of the register hitting the floor.

Then sirens. Running footsteps. Silence.

The police find you an hour later, still hiding. Curled up like a child.




Your current sanity: 59%
You dream about the day after. Not the winning itself — the day after.

You're in an apartment. Sunlight through clean windows. Coffee that didn't come from a gas station.

You wake up reaching for a coffee mug that isn't there. The absence stings.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 8 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
You slept so hard you forgot where you were for a second. That's the good kind of confusion.

The sound of hooves trotting on pavement drifts through your window, along with some distant whistling. You sit up, and through your windshield, you see a man wearing a full cowboy suit, with matching black hat and boots, and a short brown beard. 

He's riding a magnificent horse, muscular, but nimble, each step powerful, but precise. The man reaches your window, and in a deep southern accent, he begins to talk to you.

"Howdy, partner! The name's Jameson. Davey Jameson. "I happen to notice you were admiring my steed. He's a beauty, isn't he. ""You see, it's common courtesy when a cowboy rides by, "to give their mighty steed a carrot, as a way to express your gratitude for their hardwork and commitment to the job."

"You my friend, you are carrotless. That's quite a disrespectful showing towards my steed. ""My, my, this can't do at all. What if another cowboy comes by, you're just gonna disrespect their steed, too? ""Tell you what, I happen to have one spare carrot in my pouch. Take this, and be ready. ""You never know when a cowboy's gonna come trotting by."

Davey Jameson hands you his Carrot, and smiles.

"See, with this carrot in your possession, you're ready for anytime a cowboy strolls on down this road. ""Just give their steed a carrot, and they'll be very grateful."

And with that, Jameson reins his horse high into the air, gives you a yee-haw, then dashes off down the road.




Your current sanity: 72%
As you're walking along the side of the road, something catches your eye. A flash of white, darting between the bushes. A rabbit!

Without thinking, you give chase. The little creature bounds ahead of you, zigging and zagging through the underbrush with seemingly effortless grace.

You run and run, but no matter how fast you go, the rabbit stays just out of reach. Its white tail bobs mockingly in the moonlight.

Finally, you stop, hands on your knees, gasping for breath. When you look up, the rabbit is gone, vanished into the night like it was never there.

You trudge back to your wagon, defeated. But something tells you this isn't the last time you'll see that rabbit.

Getting out of the car takes three attempts. Your lower back has decided it hates you. Specifically you. Personally.

You stand in the parking lot bent at a 45-degree angle like a question mark. People stare. You deserve it.





Looking at your skinned knee, you swear you can see the bone.
Whiskers swipes at your hand when you try to pet her. No claws. But the message is clear.
You wake up to scratching noises. Something is ON your car.

You look up. A family of raccoons is making themselves at home on your roof.

Mom raccoon. Dad raccoon. Three baby raccoons. All staring at you through the windshield with those little bandit masks.

You honk the horn. They don't flinch. You honk again. The babies yawn.

You stare at each other for a full minute. They're not leaving. This is their car now.

You go back to sleep. In the morning, they've left a dead mouse on your hood. A gift? A threat? Both?



As the sun begins to set, and the stars light up in the night sky, you walk to the casino, eager to play more Blackjack. 
Each night you return. Each night, the cards wait.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 16 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
Best night's sleep in a long time. You even folded your blanket. Who are you?

The Dealer shuffles the deck. A card slips out — but it's not a playing card. It's a photograph. Old. Faded. Wallet-sized.
The Dealer snatches it up fast, but you've already seen it: a woman and a little girl standing in front of a yellow house. The woman is laughing. The girl is blowing out candles on a birthday cake.
The Dealer tucks the photo into his vest pocket without a word. His hands, always perfectly steady, have the faintest tremor.
You say nothing. Some things you don't ask about. The Dealer nods, almost imperceptibly. He appreciates the silence.
For the rest of the session, the Dealer plays differently. Quieter. Almost gentle with the cards.
Your knee has seen better days. Much, much better days.
Whiskers sits with her back to you. The cold shoulder is real.
After wandering from your vehicle, you find yourself deep in the woods. Squirrels run by and up into the trees. The sun hits every branch and casts a shadow below. And you wander on a natural path, journeying into the unknown.

As you walk along the path, you notice someone leaning against a tree in front of you. As you get closer, you notice that the person's face is blue, their eyes are bloodshot, and they don't appear to be breathing.

You begin to panic, before thinking through the situation. They're already dead, so there's nothing you can do to help them. Maybe they had some money on them? I mean, they're not gonna use it. Why shouldn't you?

Do you search the body? While this body might be the body of a rich man, judging by the situation, it's very unlikely. Plus, dead bodies tend to be unsanitary. No, this body was simply not worth searching.

You continue down the path, before the forest opens up to the main road. You follow the road back to your wagon, and sit. You rest for a while.

As the sun begins to set, and the stars light up in the night sky, you walk to the casino, eager to play more Blackjack. 
Come, sit down, we have a game to play.

You wake up and run your tongue along your teeth. All there. But the dream leaves a residue that takes hours to shake.
Your mind feels... foggy. Something isn't right.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 18 ~ ~ ~ ══════════

Whiskers has run away. They were too unhappy to stay.
Your body feels like it got a factory reset overnight. Joints? Smooth. Back? Fine. Mood? Immaculate.

On an empty lot just off the highway, a white tent flaps in the wind beside a plywood sign: REVIVAL TONIGHT - COFFEE FREE, SALVATION OPTIONAL
Inside are folding chairs, a coffee urn, and a man in shirtsleeves ladling soup into paper cups.
He notices you, smiles like he's seen worse, and lifts the ladle in greeting.
"Pastor Eli. You hungry, tired, guilty, or all three? Doesn't matter. We got enough soup for all categories."
You stay near the flap and let the steam from the soup drift your way without committing to anything holy.
"That's alright," Eli says. "I've seen people heal from doorways before."
Something's definitely wrong with your body. That's for certain.

Your current sanity: 60%
You dream about your mother's cooking. The smell fills the entire car. Garlic, butter, something on the stove.

You wake up. The car smells like old upholstery and regret. But for a second — just a second — it smelled like home.

Best night's sleep in a long time. You even folded your blanket. Who are you?

You hear hooves on asphalt before you see him. Jameson comes riding in on Thunder, but something's wrong. The horse is moving slowly, head drooping.
Jameson dismounts with effort. He looks ten years older than last time.
"Thunder ain't right. Been off his feed for three days. Won't drink water. ""Keeps lying down when he shouldn't."
The old cowboy's voice cracks. This horse is his whole world.
"I can't afford a vet. Not a real one. Those highway robbery sons of—"
He takes off his hat and holds it to his chest.
"You know anything about horses? Or know anyone who does?"

Jameson leads Thunder away on foot. The horse nuzzles against his shoulder. Even sick, they trust each other completely.

Your knee has seen better days. Much, much better days.

You can't sleep, so you walk. The city is different at this hour — quieter, more honest, the neon signs humming a frequency that only works on insomniacs and people with nothing left to protect.

You pass closed shops and sleeping houses. Everyone behind those walls has a bed. A fridge. A door that locks from the inside. You walk past all of it without slowing down, because the rhythm is the only thing that works — step, step, step, forward, one direction, don't stop.

When you get back to your car, you're tired in the right way for once. The kind of tired that actually leads to sleep.

"You've got further than I ever did. Don't make my mistakes."

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 31 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
That might have been the best sleep of your life. You feel incredible.

A glossy black limousine is quietly approaching your wagon. As you sit up from your slumber, you read 'Oswald's Optimal Outoparts' cursively engraved in gold letters on the side of the limo. Waving the vehicle down, the limo slows, then stops before you. The door opens vertically, and a large red carpet is rolled out onto the street. You watch in awe as a man, with a combover and a tuxedo, walks out before you. He coughs, then speaks.
"Why hello there! The name's Oswald, as you can see by my nametag. Do you like my bowtie? Well of course you do! It appears your limousine has broken down." Oswald pulls a gold whistle out of his pocket, and blows into it deeply. "Oh Stuart!" You watch as a bald man in a tailcoat suit, no taller than 4 feet, hobbles over to Oswald's side.
"This is Stuart! He will fix your limousine up for a fair price. Let's say, I don't know, I suppose a fair price is 500,000 dollars. Okay, the look on your face says that I'm making a big mistake. Let's try $800, and Stuart here will get you back on the road! Do you accept?" 
"Jolly good! Stuart!" You watch as the little man walks to the front of your wagon, opens the hood, and jumps in. You can't really see what's going on, but after a couple of minutes, Stuart jumps back out, covered in oil.
Your new balance is $1,703 - $800 = $903
Your car has been fixed! You can now drive around!
"Oh my Stuart! Someone got a little too excited, didn't you? Yep, you're getting a bath as soon as we get back to the shop. Thanks again, stranger, it's been a pleasure doing business with you. Your new balance is $903 + $50 = $953

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 37 ~ ~ ~ ══════════

A sharp knock on your window. You look up to see a gaunt man in a stained trench coat peering at you through the glass. His teeth are yellow, his eyes are bloodshot, and he's holding a pocket watch that looks far too expensive for someone dressed like him.

You roll down the window just a crack.

"Nice pile of cash you got there," he rasps, nodding at the money in your passenger seat. "You look like a collector. A finder of rare things."

He glances around nervously, then leans closer.

"Name's Gus. Grimy Gus, they call me. Got a little shop down on Fifth and Nowhere. ""If you ever find yourself with... unusual items... things that don't belong in the light of day... I can make them disappear. For a fair price."

He taps his nose conspiratorially.

"Collectibles, trinkets, treasures. Things you picked up on your... adventures. I don't ask questions. Just cash on the barrel."

He hands you a grimy business card through the crack in the window. It reads: "Grimy Gus's Pawn Emporium - We Buy What Others Won't"

"Come by sometime. You won't regret it. Probably."

He shuffles off into the morning mist before you can respond.

Here's what my cat whispered to me last night: "Let's embark on a journey, a meandering path not unlike the serpentine wanderings of a leaf caught in a capricious autumn breeze, which, as it dances to the silent music of nature, reminds us of the unpredictable choreography of existence. This leaf, let's call it Gerald, flutters with an elegance borne of happenstance, a fragile vessel for the whims of the wind. Gerald's journey is not linear, nor is it bound by the rigid expectations of society's ceaselessly grinding gears. Instead, Gerald twirls, dips, and soars, embracing the chaos with a grace we can only aspire to. Now, consider the ant, industrious and steadfast, a creature of purpose and communal toil. Our ant, whom we'll name Beatrice, marches diligently on her quest for sustenance, her life a testament to the virtues of hard work and persistence. Yet, in the grand tapestry of the cosmos, what is Beatrice but a speck, a mere blip on the infinite canvas of the universe? And yet, does her insignificance in the face of the vast unknown render her efforts moot? I posit that it does not, for in the grand scheme, all actions, large and small, contribute to the intricate mosaic of existence. But back to Gerald, who by now has traversed the convoluted landscapes of our imagination, touching upon the existential questions that haunt the periphery of our consciousness. What can we learn from Gerald and Beatrice? Is it their resilience, their unyielding will to persist in the face of the insurmountable odds stacked against them by the very nature of their existence? Or is it, perhaps, the simple beauty of their dance, a reminder that life, in all its complexity and confusion, offers moments of sublime beauty, fleeting and precious, to be cherished and remembered? As Gerald finally comes to rest upon the earth, joining Beatrice in the eternal cycle of life and death, we are reminded that all journeys, whether they be of leaves or ants or the human heart, are interconnected in the grand, bewildering dance of the cosmos. So, what was the point of this story, you may ask? Well, that, my friend, is entirely up to you."

You drift into a dream, and find yourself sitting at a bar inside a grand casino. Crystal chandeliers hang from the ceiling, their light dancing across marble floors. The air smells of expensive cigars and possibility.
You're chatting it up with the person next to you-someone important, though you can't quite remember who. A bartender in a crisp white shirt approaches.
"What'll it be?"
You order a drink. The bartender raises an eyebrow.
"That's gonna cost you. Expensive taste you've got."
You wave your hand dismissively. Money is no object. Not here. Not in this place.
The bartender shrugs and pours your drink. As he slides it across the bar, he says:
"Well, it's your drink after all."
You wake up, the phantom taste of bourbon lingering on your tongue.
You can almost hear the slot machines in the distance.

The sun hits your face through the windshield and you don't even mind. That's how good you feel.

You open the letter. The handwriting is the same as the notes — neat, deliberate, careful.
"Dear stranger,"
"I know you don't know who I am. That's okay. You don't need to."
"I was where you are three years ago. Same parking lot. Same car seat. Same view of the same ceiling. I played cards too — not blackjack, poker — but the principle is the same. Gambling to survive. Surviving to gamble."
"Someone helped me. I never found out who. They left me money and a chance and a note that said 'Pass it on.'"
"So I'm passing it on."
"The keys are to an apartment. Studio, nothing fancy. Rent is paid through the end of the month. After that, it's up to you. The address is on the keychain."
"I know what you're thinking. Is this real? Is this a trap? Who does this?"
"People who remember."
"The photograph was just to prove I could have hurt you. I didn't. I won't. I'm just someone who was you, once."
"Good luck. And when you can — pass it on."
It's unsigned.
You sit in your car holding a letter from a stranger who was you three years ago, and you cry. Not because you're sad. Because someone remembered what it felt like and did something about it.
The address on the keychain leads to a building on the west side. Third floor. Unit 3B. The key fits.
Inside: a studio apartment. Clean. Small. A bed, a kitchenette, a bathroom with hot water. A window that faces east — morning sun.

"The fridge has groceries. The bed has clean sheets. Welcome home — for now."
It's the nicest room you've been in since everything went wrong.
You sit on the bed. You take off your shoes. You look at the ceiling, which is not the ceiling of your car.
It's different up here.

No striped shirt. No white paint. Just a regular guy in a brown jacket. But you recognize the way he sits. The way he holds his hands. The way he watches everything.
That's the mime. That's Gerald.
You walk over. He sees you coming and tenses up, like he might run.
"Please. Sit down. Don't make it obvious."
His voice is quiet. Raspy. Like he hasn't used it in a long time.
"I was a performer. A real one. Theaters, festivals, the whole thing. ""Then I saw something I shouldn't have. Backstage at a casino. Money changing hands. ""Important hands. The kind of hands that make people disappear."
"The mime thing started as a disguise. Turns out, nobody looks twice at a mime. ""You're invisible. The perfect hiding spot is where everyone can see you."
He glances around nervously.
"I've been watching you because you're in their territory. The gambling road. ""They don't like people winning too much. Drawing attention."
Gerald nods approvingly.
"Smart. The less you know, the safer you are. Just... be careful."
He walks away. No moonwalk this time. Just a scared man in a brown jacket.
Looking at your skinned knee, you swear you can see the bone.

Your current sanity: 67%
You hear a loud crash in the distance. A tree must've fallen nearby.
As the sun begins to fall, you collect your money, and leave the warmth of your wagon. You barrel out into the wind, trudging your way to the casino.
Surprised you made it here in one piece, given the weather. It's time to bet.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 65 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
You actually want to get out of the car. This is a historic moment.

Edgar calls you over to the shed. He's sitting on an overturned bucket, looking older than usual. The shovel is leaning against the wall. His hands are resting on his knees.
"I need to ask you something. And I need you to be honest."
He holds up an envelope. Yellow. Sealed. Your name is on it.
"I wrote letters. For every drifter I've dug a hole for. ""Things I noticed about 'em. Things worth remembering. ""In case somebody comes looking someday."
"This one's yours. Don't read it now. Read it when you leave this road. ""When you're done. If you're ever done."
You take the envelope. It's heavier than paper should be.
"Good. Now, my request."
He stands up, creaking like the gate.
"I'm retiring. Can't dig like I used to. My back, my knees, ""everything's giving out. The cemetery board wants to hire a company ""with backhoes and machines. No more hand-dug graves."
"But here's the thing. The drifters' section — YOUR section — ""they don't want to maintain it. 'Not cost-effective,' they said. ""They want to bulldoze it for expansion."
His jaw tightens.
"Twenty-three people are buried back there. People nobody else remembers. ""I remember all of them. I need someone else to know they existed."
He hands you a second envelope. Inside is a list of names.
"That's them. All twenty-three. If you ever make it big — ""if those cards work out — maybe you buy some flowers once in a while."

Edgar shakes your hand. His grip is the grip of a man who has carried the weight of other people's endings for forty-five years.
"Go live, kid. That's the whole point."
You drive away from the cemetery for the last time. Your car doesn't pull toward it anymore.
Your knee has seen better days. Much, much better days.

The dream takes you back to the casino. But this time, you're not at the bar. You're sitting at a blackjack table, a drink in your hand. The ice clinks against the glass as you take a sip.
"Care to be dealt in?"
You look up at the dealer, and your blood runs cold.
The dealer looks exactly like you.
Same face. Same eyes. Same everything. They smile at you-your own smile, but somehow wrong. Twisted.
"Is something the matter?"
You shake your head. "No. Nothing's wrong."
You smile back and take a long sip of your drink. The other you deals the cards, and you play in silence, the only sound being the shuffle of cards and the clink of chips.
You wake up, unsure which one of you was the real one.Two weighted dice sit in your palm when you wake. A sticker on the bottom: 'O.O.' Oswald's lucky pair.

The line between player and dealer feels blurrier than before.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 81 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
Your body feels like it got a factory reset overnight. Joints? Smooth. Back? Fine. Mood? Immaculate.

Your eyes open. At least, you think they do.
Your eyes are open. You can see the ceiling of your car. The streetlight outside casting its orange glow. Everything is normal.
Except you can't move.
Not paralyzed-numb. Paralyzed-trapped. Your body is awake but it won't listen. Your arms are dead weight. Your legs won't respond. You can't even turn your head.
Then you see it. In the corner of your vision. Something in the back seat.
A shape. Darker than dark. It doesn't have edges — it has suggestions of edges. Like smoke that decided to sit down.
It's watching you. You can feel it watching you even though it doesn't have eyes.
Your breathing gets faster. Your heart is hammering. But you. Can't. Move.
The shape leans forward. Closer. You can feel cold radiating off it like an open freezer.
Then — snap — your body releases. You bolt upright, gasping. The back seat is empty. Nothing there. Just the dark.
You don't sleep for the rest of the night. You sit with every light on and your eyes open, watching the back seat in the rearview mirror.
Nothing comes. But the cold lingers.
The edges of your vision blur. Reality feels thin.

Looking at your skinned knee, you swear you can see the bone.

Your current sanity: 48%
You watch the wind pull twigs and branches from the trees all afternoon.
As the sun begins to fall, you collect your money, and leave the warmth of your wagon. You barrel out into the wind, trudging your way to the casino.

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 84 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
With energy. Like, real energy. Not 'I didn't die in my sleep' energy.


You wake up to the sound of tapping on your car window.
For a moment, you think you're dreaming. The morning light filters through the dusty glass, illuminating a figure standing outside your wagon.
You sit up slowly, rubbing your eyes. When you look again, the figure is still there. An old woman, dressed in a flowing white dress that seems to shimmer in the dawn light.
Her eyes are kind, but ancient. Something about her feels... familiar.
"Good morning, child. You've done well."
You crack the window open, unsure if this is real.
"Who... who are you?"
"I am the one who has watched over you since the beginning. Since that first night, when you walked into the casino with nothing but fifty dollars and a dream."
She smiles, and for a moment, you swear you see her flicker like a candle flame.
"You've accumulated a fortune through the cards. One million dollars. But wealth alone does not complete a journey."
You step out of your wagon, the cool morning air hitting your face. The woman doesn't move, simply watching you with those ancient eyes.
"To truly finish what you've started, you must visit the one who helped you get here. Your mechanic. They have something important to tell you."
"Oswald. The quiet genius. You chose his precision over all others. Your dreams whisper his name."
"Go to Oswald's Optimal Outparts this afternoon. The final piece awaits."
The woman begins to fade, her form dissolving like morning mist.
"Remember, child - you may also choose to fly away. The airport is always an option for those with means. But that choice... that choice will change everything."
And then she's gone, leaving only the faint scent of lavender and the warmth of the rising sun.
You stand there for a long moment, processing what just happened. A million dollars in your pocket, and a choice to make.
Visit Oswald at their shop... fly away from the airport... or stay here and continue gambling, now with nothing to prove.

Looking at your skinned knee, you swear you can see the bone.

Your current sanity: 49%
The afternoon sun hangs heavy in the sky. You've got $1,117,133 and a decision to make.
What would you like to do?
1. Visit Oswald's Optimal Outoparts
2. Drive to the Airport
3. Go to the Casino (Continue Playing)

You get in your wagon and drive to Oswald's Optimal Outoparts.
The shop is bustling with activity. Stuart is working on three cars at once, and Oswald is pacing around excitedly.
When he sees you, his face lights up.
"Yes yes, very good, friend, you're here!"
Oswald rushes over, practically bouncing with enthusiasm.
"Now, I know we've had our silly little chats about your, well let's not put it lightly, ""your addiction to wagering money for the possibility of turning a profit and the greater likelihood of simply losing it all, ""but this has really got me thinking."
He leans in conspiratorially.
"Perhaps, well, for me and you, there could be money to be made here."
"Now, while I leave all the hands-on activities to Stuart, I'm the brains of the business at Oswald's Optimal Outoparts. ""I'm an entrepreneur, so when I see an opportunity, I simply must take it, and by that I mean fund the hell out of it."
He gestures grandly around the shop.
"I mean, really, Stuart wouldn't be on the map as the best mechanic this side of Hollywood if it weren't for me funding his endeavors. ""So, I've come to the conclusion that, perhaps, I could help fund your endeavors, too."
Oswald grabs you by the shoulders, his eyes gleaming.
"You love gambling, yes? So why don't you rise the ranks and become the gamblee? ""You can still play all the games you know and love, like your silly little Slapjack or whatever, ""but now, we can make money off of all the stupid idiots who venture into my latest destination: A Grand Casino!"
He waves his hand dismissively.
"I haven't quite come up with the name yet, but that's where you come in. ""I know absolutely nothing about gambling, or cards, or dice, or whatever it is you do. ""But clearly there's business to be had here! And now that you're a millionaire, I trust you fully with the keys to my newest kingdom."
Oswald sticks out his hand.
"What do you say? Do you accept? Would you like to run your very own casino?"
"What? No? But... but the opportunity! The wealth! The PRESTIGE!"
Oswald sputters in disbelief, but eventually composes himself.
"Well... fine then. But you know what? I'll build it anyway! With or without you!"
His eyes narrow.
"In fact, every time you come here for upgrades, every dollar you spend... ""it's going straight into MY casino fund. You'll be funding my empire whether you like it or not!"
He cackles maniacally, then catches himself.
"Ahem. Well. Stuart can still upgrade your items, of course. But just know that your money is going to a greater purpose now."
Oswald's upgrade shop is now available. Each upgrade funds his casino project...
You leave Oswald's shop. The million dollars is still yours.

You're back at the casino table. Your double sits across from you, dealing cards with mechanical precision. You take a sip of bourbon and look at your cards.
Blackjack.
The table erupts in cheers. People you don't recognize clap you on the back, shake your hand, toast to your success. You down your drink and slam the glass on the table.
And then the ceiling opens up.
Hundred dollar bills begin to rain down from above. They fall like snow, piling up on the table, on the floor, in your lap. Everyone is laughing, grabbing at the money, stuffing their pockets.
You've never felt so rich. So powerful. So fantastic.
The other you catches your eye and smiles. "This could all be yours, you know. Forever."
You wake up with your fist clenched, as if still holding onto bills that were never there.
The promise of wealth echoes in your mind. What would you sacrifice to feel that way forever?


══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 87 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
A bird is singing outside your car. You don't want to punch it. Progress.

You're driving when your car radio turns on. By itself.
You haven't touched it. The button is right there, untouched. But the dial is glowing and static is pouring through the speakers.
Not normal static. This static has a rhythm. A pulse. Like breathing.
You reach for the dial to turn it off. The moment your finger touches it, the static stops. Clear silence. Then:
"...eighty-seven... eighty-seven... eighty-seven..."
A voice. Robotic. Monotone. Repeating a number.
Then it changes:
"...fourteen... fourteen... fourteen..."
Then back to static. Then silence. The radio turns itself off.
You sit in your car, hand still on the dial, heart pounding. The numbers echo: 87, 14.
You let the numbers fade. Probably just some trucker frequency bleeding through.
Probably.
The radio stays off for the rest of the night. But the display flickers twice when you're not looking.
Looking at your skinned knee, you swear you can see the bone.

I read this once in a magazine: "Let's embark on a journey, a meandering path not unlike the serpentine wanderings of a leaf caught in a capricious autumn breeze, which, as it dances to the silent music of nature, reminds us of the unpredictable choreography of existence. This leaf, let's call it Gerald, flutters with an elegance borne of happenstance, a fragile vessel for the whims of the wind. Gerald's journey is not linear, nor is it bound by the rigid expectations of society's ceaselessly grinding gears. Instead, Gerald twirls, dips, and soars, embracing the chaos with a grace we can only aspire to. Now, consider the ant, industrious and steadfast, a creature of purpose and communal toil. Our ant, whom we'll name Beatrice, marches diligently on her quest for sustenance, her life a testament to the virtues of hard work and persistence. Yet, in the grand tapestry of the cosmos, what is Beatrice but a speck, a mere blip on the infinite canvas of the universe? And yet, does her insignificance in the face of the vast unknown render her efforts moot? I posit that it does not, for in the grand scheme, all actions, large and small, contribute to the intricate mosaic of existence. But back to Gerald, who by now has traversed the convoluted landscapes of our imagination, touching upon the existential questions that haunt the periphery of our consciousness. What can we learn from Gerald and Beatrice? Is it their resilience, their unyielding will to persist in the face of the insurmountable odds stacked against them by the very nature of their existence? Or is it, perhaps, the simple beauty of their dance, a reminder that life, in all its complexity and confusion, offers moments of sublime beauty, fleeting and precious, to be cherished and remembered? As Gerald finally comes to rest upon the earth, joining Beatrice in the eternal cycle of life and death, we are reminded that all journeys, whether they be of leaves or ants or the human heart, are interconnected in the grand, bewildering dance of the cosmos. So, what was the point of this story, you may ask? Well, that, my friend, is entirely up to you."

After a moment, one eye cracks open to see if you're still there.

You slowly reach in with some food scraps. The opossum sniffs... then gently takes them from your hand.

It climbs out of the trash and waddles over to your car, like it already owns the place.

You name it Patches because of the distinctive marks on its fur. It immediately curls up in your backseat and falls asleep.You have befriended Patches!

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 95 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
That was some quality sleep. Five stars. Would sleep again.

You've been fighting sleep for days. Coffee. Slapping yourself. Driving with the windows down.
It doesn't matter. It comes when it wants to.
This time, you don't even realize you've fallen asleep. One moment you're driving. The next, you're parked somewhere you don't recognize, engine off, and you can't move.
The shadow fills the entire car. It's everywhere. In the mirrors, in the corners, in the gaps between the seats.
"I'm not what you think I am."

"I'm not a monster. I'm a door. Walk through me and the pain stops. The cold stops. The hunger, the loneliness, the endless, stupid cards — all of it. Gone."

"I've been watching you lose for so long. I'm offering you the only guaranteed win."

The cold is so intense your teeth are chattering. Or trying to — your jaw is locked.
Inside your head, you hear the question clearly:
"Do you accept?"

No.
Not a thought. A word. Your lips move even though your body is frozen. You force it out through locked teeth and a locked jaw.
"No."
The shadow recoils. The cold retreats. For the first time, you hear something from it that isn't confidence.
"...Interesting."

Your body releases. You sit up. The car is normal. Warm. Silent.
But in the rearview mirror, just for a second, you see it retreat into the shadows behind your headrest. And you could swear it's smiling.
Your knee has seen better days. Much, much better days.
Patches finds the driest, warmest spot in the entire car and claims it. Under your blanket. Against your side.

Your current sanity: 33%

══════════ ~ ~ ~ Morning, Day 97 ~ ~ ~ ══════════
That was some quality sleep. Five stars. Would sleep again.

Through the windshield-again-a car is parked right in front of you. You can feel your blood start to boil. What's this guy's problem? As you open the door and get out of your car, you notice the man in his bright red suit, once again peering into your trunk.

The man sees you, and walks up to you, with a pistol holstered to his waist.

"You. I'm done playing around. It's time to move. I mean it." You look down at the gun on his waist. It looks fancy, and certainly deadly.

"I wouldn't test me if I were you. It's time to go, now."

"Will you leave?" "That's great. Fantastic. But I don't believe a word that comes out of your filthy mouth. Prove it. Leave. Go away. GET OUT."

You are fueled with anger. Who is this guy, and what gives him the right to harass you? All for being homeless? No longer. You reach for the gun on his waist.

Before you get the chance to grab it, the man steps back, unholsters the pistol, then fires three shots into your chest. The glass behind you shatters, and you fall to your knees in the street.

"You should've just listened to me man! All you had to do was listen! Move, live somewhere else. Find a home, anything. But no! You just had to live in your car, like the homeless piece of shit that you are!"

The man kicks you down, and steps on your chest, causing the bullet holes to leak blood onto the concrete below you. As you feel yourself beginning to fade away, you watch the man lift his pistol to your head, and pull the trigger.
You have died!
You lasted 97 days!
You met your fate with a final balance of $123,784
